Which type of slave was often chained to the front door and acted as a watchdog for the master? ANSWER:IANITOR / OSTIARIUS BONUS:Which type of slave served as a butler for the master? ANSWER:ATRIENSIS BONUS:Which type of slave reminded the master of the names of people? ANSWER:NOMENCLATOR 
Which Epirot [EH-PEE-RIT] king, cousin of Alexander the Great, was the first to utilize elephants against the Roman army in 280 BC? ANSWER:PYRRHUS BONUS:At what battle of 280 BC did the Romans first encounter elephants? ANSWER:HERACLEA BONUS:Which consul of 275 BC defeated Pyrrhus at the Battle of Beneventum? ANSWER:(MANIUS) CURIUS DENTATUS 
Which Roman emperor’s reputed last words were “puto deus fio,” translated as I think I’m becoming a god, just before his death in 79 AD? ANSWER:VESPASIAN BONUS:Which other Roman emperor’s reputed last words were “qualis artifex pereo,” translated as what an artist dies in me? ANSWER:NERO BONUS:Which other Roman emperor’s reputed last words were “acta est fabula,” translated as the play is finished? ANSWER:AUGUSTUS 
Which law of 67 BC conferred upon Pompey the command to rid the Mediterranean of pirates? ANSWER:LEX GABINIA BONUS:Which law of 66 BC conferred upon Pompey the command to fight against the Pontic king Mithridates VI? ANSWER:LEX MANILIA BONUS:In what year, the same year as the birth of Augustus, did Mithridates VI commit suicide? ANSWER:63 BC 
Give the dictionary entry for the part of the body that is hurt by a concussion. ANSWER:CAPUT, CAPITIS, N.-HEAD BONUS:Give the dictionary entry for the part of the body that is used when you give a high-five. ANSWER:MANUS, MANUS, F.-HAND BONUS:Give the dictionary entry for the part of the body that is used to smell. ANSWER:NASUS, NASI, M. - NOSE 
What is the modern name of the city which the Romans called Mediolanum? ANSWER:MILAN BONUS:What is the modern name of the city which the Romans called Eboracum [EHBORE-RAH-KUM]? ANSWER:YORK BONUS:What is the modern name of the city which the Romans called Lutetia? ANSWER:PARIS 
Give the correct Latin form of “this poet” that would be used to translate this English sentence: Did you read the work of this poet? ANSWER:HUIUS POETAE BONUS: Now do the same as before using this English sentence: They say that this poet has written the best poem. ANSWER:HANC POETAM BONUS: Now do the same for this final English sentence: Don’t trust this poet who stole the poem from the internet. ANSWER:HUIC POETAE 
What Latin word with what meaning is at the ultimate root of cloister? ANSWER:CLAUDO - CLOSE BONUS:What Latin word with what meaning is at the ultimate root of circuit? ANSWER:EO - GO BONUS:What Latin word with what meaning is at the ultimate root of corridor? ANSWER:CURRO - RUN 
Patrician children wore gold ones while plebeian children wore leather ones. What were these items given at birth and designed to protect children from evil spirits? ANSWER:BULLA(E) BONUS:A boy gave up his bulla when he became an adult. When would a girl give up her bulla? ANSWER:WHEN SHE GOT MARRIED BONUS:In addition to the bulla, every child supposedly had a guardian spirit. What was the term for the guardian spirit of a boy? ANSWER:GENIUS 
According to Livy, an earthquake struck while the Romans were being slaughtered by the forces of Hannibal at what battle in 217 BC? ANSWER:LAKE TRASIMENE BONUS:At which earlier battle in 218 BC, a minor cavalry skirmish, did the future Scipio Africanus save the life of his father? ANSWER:TICINUS RIVER BONUS:At which other battle of 218 BC did Hannibal and Hasdrubal defeat the combined forces of the consuls, Cornelius Scipio the Elder and Tiberius Sempronius Longus? ANSWER:TREBIA (RIVER) 
Which Dalmatian slave became emperor after defeating Carinus in 285 AD and went on to establish the Tetrarchy? ANSWER:DIOCLETIAN BONUS:Who was Diocletian’s Caesar in the East who defeated Narses and captured the Persian capital of Ctesiphon [KUH-TESS-IH-FON]? ANSWER:GALERIUS BONUS:To where did Diocletian retire in 305 AD? ANSWER:SALONA / SPLIT 
What Roman god was considered first in formal prayers and his name is given to the first month of the year? ANSWER:JANUS BONUS:What unusual anatomical feature is Janus usually given when depicted in art? ANSWER:TWO HEADS/AN OLD HEAD AND YOUNG HEAD BONUS:Janus’ temple was an important building among the Romans. The opening and closing of the doors symbolized what about the Roman state? ANSWER:OPEN=WAR, CLOSE=PEACE 
Where, in the ancient city of Rome, would one find all of the following: Arch of Septimius Severus, Tabularium, Temple of Vesta, Rostra? ANSWER:FORUM (ROMANUM) BONUS: Where, in the ancient city of Rome, would one find all of the following: Circus of Flaminius, Baths of Agrippa, Horologium, Ara Pacis? ANSWER:CAMPUS MARTIUS BONUS:On what hill of Rome would one find the Arx and the Temple of Juno Moneta? ANSWER:CAPITOLINE 
Using proper idiom, translate into Latin: We give great thanks to both gods and goddess. ANSWER:MAGNAS GRATIAS ET DEIS ET DEABUS AGIMUS. BONUS:Translate into Latin: The brothers, of whom one lived, were sons of Mars and and a Vestal Virgin. FRATRES, QUORUM UNUS VIXIT/VIVEBAT, ANSWER:ERANT FILII MARTIS ET VIRGINIS VESTALIS. BONUS:Using the verb “transilio”, translate into Latin: Remus was killed after he jumped across Romulus’s wall. ANSWER:REMUS NECATUS EST/INTERFECTUS EST/NECABATUR POSTQUAM (TRANS) MURUM ROMULI TRANSILUIT. 
Burrus and Seneca the Younger were responsible for the first five good years of what Julio-Claudian emperor’s reign, although this emperor would later sing as Rome burned in 64 AD? ANSWER:NERO BONUS:Who was Nero’s obsessive mother, whom Nero tried to assassinate with a collapsible boat? ANSWER:AGRIPPINA THE YOUNGER BONUS:During Nero’s reign, which queen of the Iceni [EYE-KAY-NEE] staged a revolt in Britain which was eventually put down by Suetonius Paulinus? ANSWER:BOUDICCA
